  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d8deb917-1300-4a89-b12d-b65413df74cb'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer2250000892912402900">Before Carrie Bradshaw hit the big time in the City, she was a regular girl growing up in the suburbs of Connecticut.   <span id="freeText2250000892912402900" style="display:none">Before Carrie Bradshaw hit the big time in the City, she was a regular girl growing up in the suburbs of Connecticut. How did she turn into one of the most-read social observers of our generation?<br /><br />The Carrie Diaries opens up in Carrie's senior year of high school. She and her best friends -- Walt, Lali, Maggie, and the Mouse -- are inseparable, amid the sea of Jens, Jocks and Jets. And then Sebastian Kydd comes into the picture. Sebastian is a bad boy-older, intriguing, and unpredictable. Carrie falls into the relationship that she was always supposed to have in high school-until a friend's betrayal makes her question everything. With her high school days coming to a close, Carrie will realize it's finally time to go after everything she ever wanted.<br /><br />Rabid fans of Sex and the City will love seeing Carrie Bradshaw evolve from a regular girl into a sharp, insightful writer. They'll learn about her family background -- how she found her writing voice, and the indelible impression her early friendships and relationships left on her. We'll see what brings Carrie to her beloved New York City, where the next Carrie Diaries book will take place.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_98793756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98793756" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98793756?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780061983948" href="/book/show/7295091-the-carrie-diaries-cd">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who don't know what good YA literature is</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98793756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7091588813668892664">Have no idea why I even bothered to open this book. I actually never liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4415.Candace_Bushnell' title='Candace Bushnell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Candace Bushnell</a>'s books I've read - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1168376.Sex_and_the_City' title='Sex and the City by Candace Bushnell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sex and the City</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2186126.Lipstick_Jungle' title='Lipstick Jungle by Candace Bushnell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lipstick Jungle</a>. I guess my enjoyment of the TV show affected my judgment?<br/><br/>This novel was a drivel and I couldn't get through more than 20 pages of it. Boring, superficial, directionless high school melodrama galore with personality-less characters and no sense of time or place. I don't think even the fans of the show will enjoy the novel because Carrie of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7091370.The_Carrie_Diaries' title='The Carrie Diaries by Candace Bushnell' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Carri</a></span>
  <span id="freeText7091588813668892664" style="display:none">Have no idea why I even bothered to open this book. I actually never liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4415.Candace_Bushnell" title="Candace Bushnell" rel="nofollow noopener">Candace Bushnell</a>'s books I've read - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1168376.Sex_and_the_City" title="Sex and the City by Candace Bushnell" rel="nofollow noopener">Sex and the City</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2186126.Lipstick_Jungle" title="Lipstick Jungle by Candace Bushnell" rel="nofollow noopener">Lipstick Jungle</a>. I guess my enjoyment of the TV show affected my judgment?<br /><br />This novel was a drivel and I couldn't get through more than 20 pages of it. Boring, superficial, directionless high school melodrama galore with personality-less characters and no sense of time or place. I don't think even the fans of the show will enjoy the novel because Carrie of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7091370.The_Carrie_Diaries" title="The Carrie Diaries by Candace Bushnell" rel="nofollow noopener">The Carrie Diaries</a> had nothing to do with neurotic, clueless in men, shoe-obsesses Carrie of the show. <br /><br />Kudos to Bushnell for being smart enough to see that she, like everybody else, could cash in on exploiting the YA fiction boom. Too bad she chose to produce <i>this</i>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7091588813668892664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_180387682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180387682" />
    <a title="Megs ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5691412-megs"><img alt="Megs ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587306329p2/5691412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180387682?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megs ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megs ♥" href="/user/show/5691412-megs">Megs ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=z-2011-reads">z-2011-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180387682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13769991333742023306"><br/>If you are a SATC fan you will love this series! I think this is what most people are looking for when they read the actual book called "Sex in the City" and they are disappointed when they don't get it. This book just reads like an actual diary of a young Carrie Bradshaw, and of course since I love Carrie I love these books. She is the sweetest character ever to read about and she's fun too! I feel like she's just so real and that's what had made me a huge SATC fan for so long. I couldn't stop </span>
  <span id="freeText13769991333742023306" style="display:none"><br />If you are a SATC fan you will love this series! I think this is what most people are looking for when they read the actual book called "Sex in the City" and they are disappointed when they don't get it. This book just reads like an actual diary of a young Carrie Bradshaw, and of course since I love Carrie I love these books. She is the sweetest character ever to read about and she's fun too! I feel like she's just so real and that's what had made me a huge SATC fan for so long. I couldn't stop reading about her antics as a teen and then thinking about her as an adult and thinking "yeah, that's totally Carrie!"<br /><br /><br />Carrie isn't fully Carrie though until she's in NYC so I'm glad the series didn't spend so much time on her life before NYC. It was nice to finally have her mother's death mentioned, because in all the seasons of the show I always wondered why she never once mentioned any family members. That still doesn't clear up why she doesn't ever mention her dad or sister, but oh well...I can get over that.<br /><br /><br />I am not a fan of any of Bushnell's other writing. I like this series, but I don't think I have ever finished a single one of her other books. And yes, I have started like 3 or 4 of them always hoping I would find one I loved just because I love SATC so much. I think she's better at writing YA than adult chick-lit.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1738455129" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1738455129" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1738455129?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1738455129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16742412323054240481">Look, The Carrie Diaries is never going to win any literary awards for being a valuable exploration of teen culture, but it was a fun book. And I enjoyed reading it for it's entertainment value. <br/><br/>I've never seen one episode of Sex and the City ?? And I have only seen one or two of The Carrie Diaries but it didn't really matter. This stands alone without those other influences. <br/><br/>It basically follows Carrie Bradshaw, a school senior who's dealing with typical teenage drama - boyfriends, school prom,</span>
  <span id="freeText16742412323054240481" style="display:none">Look, The Carrie Diaries is never going to win any literary awards for being a valuable exploration of teen culture, but it was a fun book. And I enjoyed reading it for it's entertainment value. <br><br>I've never seen one episode of Sex and the City ?? And I have only seen one or two of The Carrie Diaries but it didn't really matter. This stands alone without those other influences. <br><br>It basically follows Carrie Bradshaw, a school senior who's dealing with typical teenage drama - boyfriends, school prom, mean friends, dysfunctional families and the looming, uncertain future. When she starts school, a blast from the past in the form of <i>Sebastian Kydd</i> ( the HOTTEST boy in senior year ) turns up to ruin her life, and that's basically the story<br><br> One thing I think really stood out is that, even though the drama was ridiculous and cliche, the dynamics and the aesthetic of the school and how the people and the groups interacted felt realistic. I liked that it transcended typical teenage / highschool stereotypes generally portrayed within books such as these and insisted upon the integrity and value of each person - it did not victimise or vilify one group or clique, but rather highlighted the hypocrisy and flaws of each. I liked that the faults of the protagonist and her friends were pointed out, alongside those of the "popular girls". I often find it disappointing how contemporary books dehumanise and vilify "pretty girls" generally because they are. Actually, that same concept was analysed and critiqued in The Carrie Diaries and for that I'm appreciative.<br><br>The book had a unique voice and well-rounded host of characters which I felt really fleshed it out and made it more than just a contemporary high-school romance. Carrie's voice was domineering, but she was not flawless. I liked that she was challenged by both friend and foe for her behaviours and that she was not presented as being ultimately errorless. It was really refreshing, especially in this genre which I think typically has bland protagonists who possess little or no faults. <br><br>The plot was fast moving, and it was easy reading - but not absorbing. The problems of the characters were really, really trivial. The characters issues were very <i>white, fairly wealthy teenage</i> which was fine, but not particularly engaging. It did deal with the topics it tackled well, though I felt it left the lgbt storyline hanging a bit which was disappointing - I would have liked to see it go alot more places. But other stories, including feminism, the repression of female sexuality and slut-shaming and the challenge between femininity and agency were well written. It was clear Candace Bushell places a great importance on writing gender politics and explorations and I suppose it is what she did best here. <br><br>It's a shame the writing is basic and bland, because if it'd been a bit more exciting, maybe a little more rich this book would have been better. I also which the characters had been fleshed out alot more, especially some of the central supporting characters. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ ALSO ! On a side note I was so happy Sebastian didn't end up with Carrie and he wasn't glorified because he was so shitty !! and I was so scared he'd get forgiven and have a cute romance w/ her and I was like NO  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Overall, this was a really fun read and I liked it, but it wasn't outstanding. I think for a contemporary romance though, it was really well done. Contemp. romance is a genre I usually actively avoid so that I liked this at all is amazing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474990015ra/20666693.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>ANYWAY ! I'm guessing the show and the book are reaaally different. Because everyone who watches the show LOVES Sebastian, but in the book he's ? not nice and he's not portrayed to be a good person sooo. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16742412323054240481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ Innocent Lamb ~ Forever Reading ♥ - AKA Smarties" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ Innocent Lamb ~ Forever Reading ♥ - AKA Smarties" href="/user/show/5323765-innocent-lamb-forever-reading---aka-smarties">♥ Innocent Lamb ~ Forever Reading ♥ - AKA Smarties</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer594511048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14400881250544675793">There are some books that inspire you – that make you want to do something amazing. The kind of books that make you feel like you could go anywhere you want to – That anything really is possible. Then there are the books that make you cry til you can’t no more. The type of book that people recommend you don’t read in public unless you want people to see you start crying over the book. And then there’s this book.<br/><br/>The Carrie Diaries is about a girl (Carrie) as she goes through life… finishes her la</span>
  <span id="freeText14400881250544675793" style="display:none">There are some books that inspire you – that make you want to do something amazing. The kind of books that make you feel like you could go anywhere you want to – That anything really is possible. Then there are the books that make you cry til you can’t no more. The type of book that people recommend you don’t read in public unless you want people to see you start crying over the book. And then there’s this book.<br /><br />The Carrie Diaries is about a girl (Carrie) as she goes through life… finishes her last year of high school. We learn about stuff like how she feels about being left out when all of her friends seem to be doing the deed and smoking cigarettes. This book came to me with high recommendations. I stumbled upon this book accidentally and saw all the great reviews and stuff so I thought: Heyy, let’s try this book. Yes, I have actually reached this point where nothing seems good to read. I know. (IF any of y’all feel like recommending a book to me, it would be fantastic! I’m just desperate for good books. Y’all know what to do.)<br /><br />This book?<br /><br />NEVER AGAIN.<br /><br />The characters – there was something I just didn’t like about them.<br /><br />The plot – Ughh… No Way. This book just reminded me about why high school is so horrible at times.<br /><br />The main character – Carrie was okay, I guess. Not the best, nor was she one I particularly liked, but I was okay with her.<br /><br />Sebastian Kydd – I’m not even going to comment on this one.<br /><br />So yep: 1 star. Sorry.<br /></span>

<div id="review_127580374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127580374" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4383168-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520024353p2/4383168.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127580374?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/4383168-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4383168-amy?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4383168-amy?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127580374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13938621657585448028">I have plenty of guilty pleasures and even though I call them that, I try not to feel too guilty about them. (Life's too short, right?) One of my biggest pleasures is reading teen and pre-teen literature. Another is the ridiculous joy that is Sex and the City. So reading The Carrie Diaries was like combining the two in one ultimate dream! <br/><br/>Well, not quite. But it was fun. <br/><br/>There are a few oddly glaring inconsistencies between the book and the TV series, however. In the series, she re-dates her hig</span>
  <span id="freeText13938621657585448028" style="display:none">I have plenty of guilty pleasures and even though I call them that, I try not to feel too guilty about them. (Life's too short, right?) One of my biggest pleasures is reading teen and pre-teen literature. Another is the ridiculous joy that is Sex and the City. So reading The Carrie Diaries was like combining the two in one ultimate dream! <br /><br />Well, not quite. But it was fun. <br /><br />There are a few oddly glaring inconsistencies between the book and the TV series, however. In the series, she re-dates her high school boyfriend who she went to prom with... she doesn't actually go to the prom in the book. I'm sure there's stuff mentioned about how Carrie in the series is an only child raised by a single mother yet in the book her mum has died and left her dad to raise her and her two sisters (!!) Also, she's bizarrely an excellent cook, whereas in the show it's often mentioned how she never cooks and uses her oven to store sweaters. <br /><br />It's a teen book, really, despite the peppering of expletives. Don't read it expecting it to be a grown up novel! You can probably already tell whether you'll like this or not: it's more or less what you're expecting. I enjoyed it, though. <br /><br />And I especially liked the very last sentence. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13938621657585448028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1234286591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1234286591" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2917700-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483254339p2/2917700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9361271294611934917">So i picked up this book for a bit of a laugh thinking it was going to be trashy fun. SURPRISE: It was actually really good?<br/><br/>Disclaimer: I haven’t seen an episode of Sex in the City. I’ve seen the first movie but that’s pretty much it. I’ve also seen the first few episodes from when they adapted this book into a show and barring a few things, this book is nothing like that. <br/><br/>Carrie is an amazing character. Sure she’s a teenager and sometimes she screws up, but she’s all about girl power and doesn’</span>
  <span id="freeText9361271294611934917" style="display:none">So i picked up this book for a bit of a laugh thinking it was going to be trashy fun. SURPRISE: It was actually really good?<br /><br />Disclaimer: I haven’t seen an episode of Sex in the City. I’ve seen the first movie but that’s pretty much it. I’ve also seen the first few episodes from when they adapted this book into a show and barring a few things, this book is nothing like that. <br /><br />Carrie is an amazing character. Sure she’s a teenager and sometimes she screws up, but she’s all about girl power and doesn’t take shit from boys about how girls are “boring” or “stupid”. While sometimes she drops the ball when she’s told she’s “not like other girls”, overall she’s fab.<br /><br />I pretty much hated Sebastian from the get go. He was just too slick and perfect. He pretty much had a neon “douchebag” sign floating over his head. But sometimes smart girls fall for the wrong guys. Sebastian wasn’t the only character I wanted to slap silly, especially towards the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[How in the world does Lali feel zero remorse for what she’s done? How can it be so easy for her to turn her back on a lifelong friendship without giving a fuck? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, this book was a lot better than I expected.</span>

<div id="review_127783421" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127783421" />
    <a title="Jessica  Sinn (Books and Trouble)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4459105-jessica-sinn-books-and-trouble"><img alt="Jessica  Sinn (Books and Trouble)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476991148p2/4459105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127783421?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica  Sinn (Books and Trouble)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica  Sinn (Books and Trouble)" href="/user/show/4459105-jessica-sinn-books-and-trouble">Jessica  Sinn (Books and Trouble)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127783421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6857164604856214214">Finally Candace Bushnell answers the questions that have plagued diehard Sex in the City fans ever since Carrie Bradshaw sipped her first pink cosmo: How did Carrie hit the big time as a newspaper columnist in New York City? What spurred her fascination with bad boys and high fashion? And most importantly – how did she meet her fabulous trio of gal pals?<br/><br/>Considering this book is classified as young adult, many Sex in the City fans will dismiss it as a dumbed-down “little Carrie” story filled with</span>
  <span id="freeText6857164604856214214" style="display:none">Finally Candace Bushnell answers the questions that have plagued diehard Sex in the City fans ever since Carrie Bradshaw sipped her first pink cosmo: How did Carrie hit the big time as a newspaper columnist in New York City? What spurred her fascination with bad boys and high fashion? And most importantly – how did she meet her fabulous trio of gal pals?<br /><br />Considering this book is classified as young adult, many Sex in the City fans will dismiss it as a dumbed-down “little Carrie” story filled with high school hijinks and insipid mean-girl melodrama. But don’t be fooled, this book runs much deeper than – gasp! – the plotlines in the TV series and the movies.<br /><br />Before donning Monolos and hobnobbing with A-listers at trendy Manhattan hotspots, Carrie Bradshaw was a small town girl who dreamed of being a writer and jumping on a train toward the bright lights of Manhattan. Detailing the hardships young Carrie encountered after her mother’s death – a back-story barely touched upon in the series – Bushnell reveals how the insecure teen depended more on her friends than her widowed father to maneuver her way through the emotional minefield of adolescence.<br /><br />In this much-anticipated prequel, Bushnell offers a glimpse into the origins of Carrie’s outlandish fashion sense and penchant for tall, dark and dangerous men. Sebastian Kydd, a James Dean kind of bad boy, most certainly foreshadows Carrie’s rocky road ahead with the notorious Mr. Big.<br /><br />A refreshing departure from shallow plotlines surrounding product placement, over-the-top weddings and decadent trips to Abu Dhabi, “The Carrie Diaries” offers a coming-of-age story that gives “our girl” a bit more substance. Fans in need of a Sex in the City fix will love seeing Carrie evolve from an awkward teen into a quick-witted, insightful writer.<br /><br />Although I was hoping Bushnell would give readers a taste of Carrie’s early beginnings with Miranda, Samantha and Charlotte, she does reveal the young fashonista’s road to New York City and serendipitous encounter with a certain PR bad girl. Oh Candace, please tell me you’re writing a sequal!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6857164604856214214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sofía Cividanes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15378296-sof-a-cividanes"><img alt="Sofía Cividanes" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/499972620?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofía Cividanes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofía Cividanes" href="/user/show/15378296-sof-a-cividanes">Sofía Cividanes</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer499972620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17009129757919419522">Making the decision of picking a book to read during the Christmas break was not easy although in the end, basing myself on other people’s recommendations, I ended up reading this novel by Candace Bushnell, The Carrie Diaries. This novel is all about Carrie’s coming of age and the course of the twelfth grade with its ups and downs. <br/>Throughout the book, the protagonist, Carrie encounters many obstacles. These issues vary from having a problematic sister to an unfaithful boyfriend that at points m</span>
  <span id="freeText17009129757919419522" style="display:none">Making the decision of picking a book to read during the Christmas break was not easy although in the end, basing myself on other people’s recommendations, I ended up reading this novel by Candace Bushnell, The Carrie Diaries. This novel is all about Carrie’s coming of age and the course of the twelfth grade with its ups and downs. <br />Throughout the book, the protagonist, Carrie encounters many obstacles. These issues vary from having a problematic sister to an unfaithful boyfriend that at points make her life a living hell. <br />In my opinion, I think this book is very recommendable to any girl in high school mainly because the things Carrie goes through are things that I’ve seen amongst my friends or people from the grades above and when reading the book, I could sometimes relate. For example, Carrie fights a lot with her younger sister and so do I. Also, it’s very amusing to read the issues she has between friends because that’s something almost everybody goes through.<br />What I liked the most about the book is being able to completely get to know the protagonist, Carrie and imagine her in my mind. I guess that if there had been a movie about the book, it would have been harder to make up the faces of the characters in my mind. While reading it, the conclusions I drew from Carrie’s character is that she’s just a girl like any other. I liked that a lot because in some books, the characters are somewhat fictional and it makes it hard to relate but this time it was different and it made me enjoy the reading a lot more. On the other hand, it was also really interesting to see how well written and realistic is the betrayal of her best friend because it’s basically the bomb that you’re waiting for to explode all along the novel.<br />Overall, I think this is a very interesting book and personally, I don’t enjoy reading but I surely did enjoy this book. I recommend it to every teenage girl and I hope they enjoy it as much as I did.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17009129757919419522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7468358808987159910" style="display:none">So far, this is not the Carrie I know...<br /><br />Indeed, these are not the droids you're looking for. If you were a fan of the TV series (which, let's face it, is the only reason this book got published), this book is not going to introduce you to socialite and writer Carrie Bradshaw: The Early Years.<br /><br />What exists here is either a massive retcon of the tv series, or author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4415.Candace_Bushnell" title="Candace Bushnell" rel="nofollow noopener">Candace Bushnell</a> decided that the Carrie she wrote the original <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7455.Sex_and_the_City" title="Sex and the City by Candace Bushnell" rel="nofollow noopener">Sex and the City</a> had a very different past that she'[d never covered. And (perhaps sadly), I can tell you where all of these things are refuted in the tv show.<br /><br />This isn't a BAD book by any means, but take out the last chapter, and/or change some names, and it could be any book about any girl in Connecticut in the 80s.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107593165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9722031382507037559">At least 100 pages too long and exceedingly pointless. I have no idea what Bushnell was trying to do with this. It's too slow and inwardly-focused for the Sweet Valley High crowd, and as a teen novel for adults (Secret History, Prep, etc.), it fails miserably, with the fact that there is almost no character development whatsoever being one of numerous flaws. All of the characters are 2-dimensional, nearly interchangeable. I kept comparing the Carrie in this book to the Carrie of the show (which </span>
  <span id="freeText9722031382507037559" style="display:none">At least 100 pages too long and exceedingly pointless. I have no idea what Bushnell was trying to do with this. It's too slow and inwardly-focused for the Sweet Valley High crowd, and as a teen novel for adults (Secret History, Prep, etc.), it fails miserably, with the fact that there is almost no character development whatsoever being one of numerous flaws. All of the characters are 2-dimensional, nearly interchangeable. I kept comparing the Carrie in this book to the Carrie of the show (which I'm a big fan of), then having to remind myself that Bushnell has almost nothing to do w/ the tv series (which was "loosely" based on Bushnell's original SATC book), and that the Carrie in this book should be viewed as a stand-alone character. But as such, there is basically nothing to her. She's likeable - smart, witty, courageous - but her strengths only make it all the more improbable that she would end up in some of the situations that we find her in. I was hoping for a guilty pleasure in reading this, but it was more like a total waste of time.</span>

  <span id="freeText2045641146195647070" style="display:none">Reviewed by Angela S. for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />THE CARRIE DIARIES follows Carrie Bradshaw pre-Sex and the City.<br /><br />Seventeen-year-old Carrie is just beginning her senior year in high school, and like all girls she falls for the gorgeous bad boy, Sebastian Kydd. Before long, Carrie and Sebastian are a couple - and the envy of the popular girls, who harass Carrie and make her life harder than it needs to be.<br /><br />Besides Carrie's hot-and-cold relationship with Sebastian, she also has to deal with a huge secret her best friend, Walt, is keeping, and a betrayal that threatens to ruin a lifelong friendship in an instant.<br /><br />Fans of Sex and the City will enjoy this novel, as it gives a lot of information on Carrie's family life and what inspired her to become a writer. It also recounts how it is that Carrie arrived in New York all those years ago, which ties it in nicely with both Candace Bushnell's adult novels and the show.</span>

  <span id="freeText112374949410857903" style="display:none">I didn't expect much from this book but, hey! it was actually good! I mean, I never read or watch Sex and The City before. And I actually think, "A book about Carrie Bradshaw? Really?" Boy, I was wrong!<br /><br />The book tells us about Carrie Bradshaw's final year of school, how she desperately want to be a writer, how she faced boyfriend problems, friendship problems &amp; family problems. Written in Carrie's perspective, I think Carrie is a very likeable &amp; down to earth character.<br /><br />Carrie's life may seemed perfect -good grades, beautiful, strong friendships, etc. But actually, it's not. I like how Bushnell portrayed the father-daughter relationship here -it's very real! Besides, she didn't forget to put it. Teenagers life wasn't all about boys &amp; friendship, they could be about family. And Bushnell mixed all those. Oh! And not to forget, about the future. In this book, Carrie was rejected by the New School - her favourite school and yes, many of us faced that too.<br /><br />I also like how Carrie solved things up in this book. And how she ended up to be friends with her nemesis. <br /><br />Sebastian's really a jerk - I know it from the start. He reminds me of Daniel Cleaver from Bridget Jones's Diary. And George does reminds of Mark Darcy. I don't know how, but they just do. <br /><br />Anyway, this book is hilarious and fun to read. I might give 4 stars here if I read it in one sitting. But I couldn't. Whenever I want to finish this book, something important just came up. *sigh*</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383636876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6023282626875624654">THE CARRIE DIARIES is a coming of age novel regarding a young, small town girl with big dreams. Meet Carrie Bradshaw, before the glamour, before the glitz and before Sex and the City. Carrie starts out as an eager adolescent, mesmerized by pop culture, fashion and literature. However, with her senior year looming over her and her youngest sister constantly acting out, she finds it hard to find the perfect balance between her passions, boyfriend, and the expectations of her father. With the hunch</span>
  <span id="freeText6023282626875624654" style="display:none">THE CARRIE DIARIES is a coming of age novel regarding a young, small town girl with big dreams. Meet Carrie Bradshaw, before the glamour, before the glitz and before Sex and the City. Carrie starts out as an eager adolescent, mesmerized by pop culture, fashion and literature. However, with her senior year looming over her and her youngest sister constantly acting out, she finds it hard to find the perfect balance between her passions, boyfriend, and the expectations of her father. With the hunch that her boyfriend and best friend together are untrustworthy when she is not around, the stress seems to crack down on Carrie. She has dreams of becoming a world renowned writer, but her father has different plans. He is certain that his daughter will be attending Brown in the fall, following in his footsteps to become a scientist. As she formulates a plan to get into a summer writing program, and persuade her father to let her attend, a continuous flow of hurdles present themselves. Her friends change, and through events that happen, she finally see’s who her real friends are, and who are pleased in her social and mental downfall. And as she tries to conquer all her problems, not everyone is left happy with her decisions. The characters and the story line show relevance to a teenage audience, making it a interesting and recommended read for those in a similar place. ‘The Carrie Diaries’ is an excellent read and perfect fro those who loved Sex and the City.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6023282626875624654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Cheren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31529381-cheren"><img alt="Cheren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411934389p2/31529381.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1046412224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6046603455513435381">The Carrie Diaries, is the prequel to the epic book series, Sex and the City. This book takes place during the iconic 1980's, following Carrie as she tries to juggle her aspirations, dreams, and the social burdens that accompany high school. Carrie is very strong willed. She isn't afraid to go after what she wants, but she has her weak moments, as every high schooler does. What I enjoyed most about this book, is that it doesn't lie to the readers. It doesn't paint this beautiful picture of high </span>
  <span id="freeText6046603455513435381" style="display:none">The Carrie Diaries, is the prequel to the epic book series, Sex and the City. This book takes place during the iconic 1980's, following Carrie as she tries to juggle her aspirations, dreams, and the social burdens that accompany high school. Carrie is very strong willed. She isn't afraid to go after what she wants, but she has her weak moments, as every high schooler does. What I enjoyed most about this book, is that it doesn't lie to the readers. It doesn't paint this beautiful picture of high school life, and it doesn't paint a cliché one either. This book doesn't skimp on the traditional adventures of high school. There are the catty girls. There are best friends that stab each other in the back. There are boys that make a girl believe that they'll be together forever, only to betray her in the end. It deals with the real issues of growing up, and getting hurt, and this book was so brilliant because how Carrie deals with all these problems, can be an inspiration to all struggling high schoolers. She lets her emotions rule her and reacts in ways not unlike how girls do today, which makes this book relatable. But Carrie's ability to pick herself up, brush herself off, and keep on smiling despite the dark clouds above her head, makes her a role model for women, young and old, to look up to. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6046603455513435381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8254848404794854097" style="display:none">I'm a really big Sex and the City fan...but I am from Jamaica (the Caribbean) and our cultures being so different and smaller societies being so much more conservative, and I hadnt done as much travelling to really understand half of what the show was really about....I wasn't allowed to watch HBO (or cable fro that matter..with its profanity, nudity and explicit sexual contents) until well into my late teens. By the time I really got into watching these 4 girls and know about their many dating and life troubles...I had already had too many Miss Adventures of my own!! Now I'm old enough to appreciate how in my life I could identify with each of the characters and their life changes (even in both Movies/Motion Pictures) and I began to wonder what was/would Carrie's teenage years look like (I identify most with her than the other 3...).<br /><br />The writing was entertaining and I'm glad it was done somewhat in similar fashion to the show's narrative musing...It was clever and amusing but serious when it needed to be, albeit a bit obsessive on some points (just like a teenage girl right???lol). It did do the necessary introductions to Carrie's very fullsome all inclusive lifestyle...I enjoyed it fully!!<br /></span>

Carrie Bradshaw is one of my all-time favorite literary and television characters, fashion icons, and "every" woman.<br /><br />This novel is actually a prequel to "Sex and the City", and introduces us to Carrie as she begins her senior year of high school. We see Carrie as she struggles to find her writing voice, gently experiments with fashion, and questions her own place in the small town where she has grown up. Friends, dating, family drama, peer pressure, you name it - Carrie experiences it all (and with her usual candor, optimism, and sensitivity). <br /><br />A fabulous coming-of-age story about a girl on the brink of becoming a woman, and doing it on her own terms.<br /><br />**warning**<br />Although it is marked as YA Fiction, this book contains strong language, sexual references, and drug/alcohol use.</span>

<div id="review_859556453" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859556453" />
    <a title="Shinjini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27433269-shinjini"><img alt="Shinjini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422875208p2/27433269.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/859556453?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shinjini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shinjini" href="/user/show/27433269-shinjini">Shinjini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27433269-shinjini?shelf=reviews-written">reviews-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27433269-shinjini?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer859556453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10574753579422980285">I had never picked up any of Candace Bushnell's books, neither had I ever watched the Sex and the City drama series during its original run on TV. I did hear good reviews about the first season of The Carrie Diaries series and had gotten this book around the time it was airing. <br/><br/>I wasn't able to form a strong opinion about the book as I went in and by the end of it, not much had changed. There were some things I liked about the story and certain things that were clear misses for me. <br/><br/><b>What I Didn't</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10574753579422980285" style="display:none">I had never picked up any of Candace Bushnell's books, neither had I ever watched the Sex and the City drama series during its original run on TV. I did hear good reviews about the first season of The Carrie Diaries series and had gotten this book around the time it was airing. <br /><br />I wasn't able to form a strong opinion about the book as I went in and by the end of it, not much had changed. There were some things I liked about the story and certain things that were clear misses for me. <br /><br /><b>What I Didn't Like:</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>1) Character Development (or lack thereof):</b>
</i> I hated the fact that the characters were written as purely black or purely white. There were no layers to some characters and I did not appreciate the lack of reasoning behind certain actions and steps taken by some characters. The lead character also came off as immature. Now, I do realize that this is a YA book and this is somewhat common in YA, but considering Carrie Bradshaw, later in her life, becomes a person that people come to for advice, it would have been more believable had she shown some wisdom here too.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>2) Pace:</b>
</i> This book was definitely not a page turner for me. I was struggling in the first half because nothing was happening and I was just bored. The lack of depth in the characters just made it that much worse. Near the end though, it got better and I finished the last 40% in one sitting.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>3) Boy Trouble:</b>
</i> I dislike seeing well-educated, smart girls turning into putty when there's a boy around. The main character and some secondary characters behaved so irrationally because of the main male character. Or rather, he just forced people to behave like a nut-case. I think it is really unhealthy for young girls to read about characters like these and since this book is targeted to the teen audience, it would probably have been wiser to have at least one sensible main character. Although I must admit, the character of Roberta “The Mouse” was pretty reasonable but she was not around long enough.<br /><br /><b>What I Liked:</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>1) Length:</b>
</i> It was a short book and pretty easy to read. Only if the pace was faster, I would have enjoyed it some more.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>2) LGBT representation:</b>
</i> Considering the book was set in the 80s, I wasn't expecting it but I was happy to see the representation. One of the main characters came out to the friend group and it was handled very well. I was shocked at the backlash by some of the other characters, though.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>3) Female Ambition:</b>
</i> I was happy to see that near the end, the main character showed some maturity and followed her heart, refusing to let the men in her life tell her what to do. Hopefully, this would be explored and written more about in the next book.<br /><br />The pace picked up around the 65% mark and I stayed up until the wee hours of the night to finish the story. A lot happened in the last few chapters and I couldn't keep the book down. I really liked that and that's what brought my rating up to 3. I'd probably pick up the next book in the series sometime in the future.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10574753579422980285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1363258-kris"><img alt="Kris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408895564p2/1363258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107091298?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kris" href="/user/show/1363258-kris">Kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1363258-kris?shelf=brookhaven-fall-2010">brookhaven-fall-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107091298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1875368339140568245">Candance Bushnell has written a fantastic prequel to her Sex And The City. Carrie Bradshaw is a senior in high school in a small town. She dreams of being a writer, but is struggling to find her voice and wondering if it is all just an unrealistic dream. Carrie has a cast of characters who are her friends, such as the smart Mouse, dramatic Maggie and competitive Lali. She falls in love with the dreamy new boy, Sabastian Kydd. Carrie wonders how much she is willing to compromise to be with him. W</span>
  <span id="freeText1875368339140568245" style="display:none">Candance Bushnell has written a fantastic prequel to her Sex And The City. Carrie Bradshaw is a senior in high school in a small town. She dreams of being a writer, but is struggling to find her voice and wondering if it is all just an unrealistic dream. Carrie has a cast of characters who are her friends, such as the smart Mouse, dramatic Maggie and competitive Lali. She falls in love with the dreamy new boy, Sabastian Kydd. Carrie wonders how much she is willing to compromise to be with him. We watch her love of vintage clothes unfold as she searches through her mother’s things (her mother died recently after a long illness) and dons genuine go go boots from the 70′s for the first day of school. “I figure the boots have had a much more interesting life than I have.”<br /><br />Watching Carrie develop into the character I know and love so well was a joy! She is a smart (takes Calculus and her dad wants her to be a scientist), independent character hopefully teens will latch onto. Unlike Bushnell’s more mature material, The Carrie Diaries are age appropriate and written for the teen audience. Page 109 make me cheer out loud. Carrie talked about how she wanted to be rescued by the feminist writer, Mary Gordon Howard. That experience was humiliating and she was ashamed. “But that was a long time ago. I’m not that girl anymore. I don’t need to feel ashamed. And I don’t need to be rescued either.”<br /><br />Carrie finds her writing voice after a particularly humiliating encounter with the resident mean girl, Donna LaDonna. She writes a column for the school paper under a pen name about Queen Bees. At that moment I heard Sarah Jessica Parker’s inner monologue voice come out as she does when she writes in column in the series. Carrie learns about the power of the written word and how the reaction is not always what you expect.<br /><br />Another favorite moment of mine is on page 384 when she says, “I have this theory: If you forgive someone, they can’t hurt you anymore.”<br /><br />This is a great read! I recommend it for both teens and adults. I love the last line in the book. It will make you smile! In my dream world, Candance Bushnell will also write The Samantha Diaries, The Miranda Diaries and The Charlotte Diaries.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1875368339140568245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_111326833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111326833" />
    <a title="Nancy/girlsinthestacks.com" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3067672-nancy-girlsinthestacks-com"><img alt="Nancy/girlsinthestacks.com" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326640763p2/3067672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111326833?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy/girlsinthestacks.com" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy/girlsinthestacks.com" href="/user/show/3067672-nancy-girlsinthestacks-com">Nancy/girlsinthestacks.com</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111326833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13518612331212794894">Candace Bushnell’s latest book, The Carrie Diaries, is aimed at the Young Adult market as a chance to “Meet Carrie before Sex and the City.” I love Sex and the City (the TV show) so I wanted to read this story, but I had to wonder – would this story for teens be as frank and explicit as the show? <br/><br/>As it turns out, it is frank but not explicit, which I think really rings true to YA (and adult) readers everywhere who are tired of idealized heroines who don’t cuss or have sex. Even if you are not a </span>
  <span id="freeText13518612331212794894" style="display:none">Candace Bushnell’s latest book, The Carrie Diaries, is aimed at the Young Adult market as a chance to “Meet Carrie before Sex and the City.” I love Sex and the City (the TV show) so I wanted to read this story, but I had to wonder – would this story for teens be as frank and explicit as the show? <br /><br />As it turns out, it is frank but not explicit, which I think really rings true to YA (and adult) readers everywhere who are tired of idealized heroines who don’t cuss or have sex. Even if you are not a SATC fan, this young Carrie Bradshaw is a character you can really care about. She’s a small town girl who dreams of being a writer, is fiercely loyal to her friends, has a bold sense of fashion and is looking for romance. <br /><br />This coming of age story chronicles Carrie’s senior year of high school. She applied at Brown, but was devastated when rejected for a summer writing seminar in New York. Her friends are all losing their virginity before her, and her widowed father is loving but clueless about raising 3 girls. When she meets and begins to date the new boy in school, Sebastian Kydd, she earns the ire of a group of cheerleaders called “the Jens” and their leader, Donna La Donna. Then her best friend’s betrayal changes everything. <br /><br />I connected with Carrie’s story in many ways. I loved reliving the soaring highs and the devastating lows of first love. The stickier question is why you change your essential self in order to please the one you love? Carrie remembers her feminist mother and finds inner reserves of strength from that. The eighties references (I’m dating myself here) I giggled at, and the longing to grow up and live your dream I definitely remembered. The jealousy between girls – even best friends – was a sadder but realistic part of high school I also remembered well.<br /><br />This book is such an engaging and interesting read. Carrie’s voice is strong and endearing. You can see the beginnings of the fabulous fashionista, successful writer and best friend to Charlotte, Samantha and Miranda that she becomes. The last line in the book made me howl with laughter – and I am not a howler! I recommend this book for young adults and adults alike, and all fans of chick lit.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13518612331212794894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_104629675" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104629675" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396911-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104629675?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/1396911-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">SATC and Teen Drama fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer104629675&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104629675" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17185125954464285416"> I admit I am a rabid fan of Sex and the City so of course when a prequel book came out I had to get it to get my Carrie fix before the new movie came out. Overall a very good teen drama type read that is pretty true to character. I tended to picture a cross among various SJP characters such as the ones she played in "Square Pegs" and "Girls Just Want to Have Fun" mixed with the Carrie we know and love. I liked it enough that I hope Bushnell continues the pre-SATC saga. <br/><br/>That being said there are</span>
  <span id="freeText17185125954464285416" style="display:none"> I admit I am a rabid fan of Sex and the City so of course when a prequel book came out I had to get it to get my Carrie fix before the new movie came out. Overall a very good teen drama type read that is pretty true to character. I tended to picture a cross among various SJP characters such as the ones she played in "Square Pegs" and "Girls Just Want to Have Fun" mixed with the Carrie we know and love. I liked it enough that I hope Bushnell continues the pre-SATC saga. <br /><br />That being said there are a few inconsistancies with some of the plot points (at least relative to the series, I have not read the book) that left me irritated. I'll address them below, so consider this your spoiler alert. <br /><br />In The Diaries, Carrie is being raised by her widower scientist father along with two sisters. For all I know this is the case in the book, but in the series she and her mother were abandonded by her father when she was 3 or so (this is dicussed as the reason she has problems with men in season 4 when her Vogue editor hits on her to help Carrie work out her Daddy issues). In the book she has issues with boys because her mother died when she was young and wasn't able to teach her womanly whiles. I also think it's weird we never heard about the sisters in the series, I know the point was that it was all about friendships as opposed to families, but we know about Charlette's brother and Miranda's sister and brother, but not Carrie's. The closest thing to the mention of a sister is when Carrie pretends to be her sister answering the phone because she was rude to the Russian. <br /><br />That last inconsistancy is relative to SATC2. In the movie she meets Samantha where she was tending bar. In the book she has gotten Samantha's number from a classmate. Samantha is already working in PR and Carrie calls her on her first day in the NYC</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pPlKaRURGloM9cIUhoonoLKb6LPHdJn9lS6sUFLaDOlLROX7Q4pkVd2tPihwO0o1rZorPcu71unRD+dThJER9w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ov4mf6FswZTfC86vwKDwjCX2kxg1JpeCcGn+c2GkE79NQ4nt9/e/mw5TMpM2EZ0ZOvdQljnp2JY0SLVwt+8OoQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText15064701691987600693" style="display:none"><b>Candace Bushnell</b> is the critically acclaimed, international best-selling author of <i>Killing Monica</i>, <i>Sex and the City</i>, <i>Summer and the City</i>, <i>The Carrie Diaries</i>, <i>One Fifth Avenue</i>, <i>Lipstick Jungle</i>, <i>Trading Up</i>, and <i>Four Blondes</i>. <i>Sex and the City</i>, published in 1996, was the basis for the HBO hit series and two subsequent blockbuster movies. <i>Lipstick Jungle</i> became a popular television series on NBC, as did <i>The Carrie Diaries</i> on the CW. </span>
